**Viral loop ┬À per-IP rate limit on the public `/d/<slug>` page ÔÇö DONE (closes the one deferred gate before heavy promotion).** The shareable-decision page was the only public, unauthenticated read surface with no rate limit (the explicitly-deferred item from the 2026-06-16 share-security re-verification). Added a per-IP cap on the anonymous `getPublicDecision` read: 600 reads / 1-hour rolling window per client IP, mirroring KI-10's ingest limiter shape. The guard runs _before_ the DB read, keyed on `cf-connecting-ip` (Cloudflare-set ÔåÆ unspoofable on the Workers deploy; `x-forwarded-for`/`x-real-ip` are dev fallbacks). It is **fail-open** by construction (any DB error or unresolved IP ÔåÆ the read proceeds), so the limiter can never make a legitimate shared link 404; a blocked caller sees the same "not available" page as a private/missing slug, which is fine because slugs are unguessable CSPRNG (this is anti-DoS, not anti-enumeration). The window/limit math is a pure `decidePublicReadRateLimit` with 7 `bun test` cases (boundary at exactly windowMs, increment, block + retry-after, count-overshoot race, custom params); the DB wrapper uses `onConflict: "client_ip"` on the UNIQUE key so a window reset UPDATEs rather than inserting a duplicate. Bundle-safety verified: the service-role `supabaseAdmin` import (a lazy Proxy) compiles into the server-only chunk and leaks nothing to the client bundle (grep-confirmed). **Verification:** `bun test` 108 green (+7), `bun run build` green, client bundle clean of `SERVICE_ROLE`/the limiter table. **Gate:** the migration applies on the next Lovable sync (until then `public_decision_rate_limits` doesn't exist, the checker fails open, and reads are unlimited ÔÇö exactly today's behavior). Built file-disjoint from the parallel M-A Slice 2 (Today) lane. **Files:** `supabase/migrations/20260616190000_p3_public_decision_ratelimit.sql`, `src/lib/decisions-ratelimit.server.ts` (+`.test.ts`) new; `src/lib/decisions-share.functions.ts` (guard + IP resolver) edited; `docs/features/shareable-decisions.md`, `active-task.md`, this log.

**M-C pricing and paywall foundation: plan tier + entitlements + billing surface + gated Stripe (BUILT, working tree).** The monetization foundation from v7 section 9. `workspaces` gains `plan_tier` (free/pro/team, default free), the two stripe ids, and `plan_updated_at`, with a `BEFORE INSERT OR UPDATE` trigger (`protect_workspace_billing_columns`) that makes the billing columns service-role-write-only: a non-service-role INSERT is forced to free with no billing ids, a non-service-role UPDATE preserves the prior values. So a free user cannot self-grant a paid plan by PATCHing or INSERTing the column directly (the `ws owner manage` RLS policy is FOR ALL, so both write paths had to be guarded, not just UPDATE). Pure `src/lib/entitlements.ts` (free does not persist memory, retention 14 days; pro and team persist forever; Critic-everywhere + team-only shared memory / approval lanes) with 9 `bun test` cases and a fail-safe `normalizePlanTier` that defaults unknown values to free. `src/lib/billing.functions.ts`: `getBillingState` (authed, pre-migration tolerant, defaults free) + owner-only `createCheckoutSession` (Stripe Checkout via the REST API over fetch, no SDK dependency, gated on `STRIPE_SECRET_KEY` + a price id). `src/routes/api/stripe/webhook.ts` verifies the Stripe HMAC signature with Web Crypto + a replay window (accepts any of multiple v1 sigs for key rotation) and maps subscription state to `plan_tier` via the service-role client (gated on `STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET`; a 200 no-op until configured). A Settings -> Plan tab (`BillingTab`) shows the current plan, the three tiers, and an owner-only Upgrade CTA that degrades to an honest "billing not connected yet" until keys exist (nothing is charged). **Deferred on purpose:** the memory-expiry enforcement (free memory expiring) is kept out of this lane to stay file-disjoint from the parallel M-A Slice 2 (Today) work; it lands as a clean additive follow-up (an `expires_at` + a recall-path filter) after Slice 2. **Verification:** `bun test` 117 green (+9), `bun run build` green, client bundle grep-clean of `STRIPE_SECRET_KEY` / service-role; a focused adversarial security review verdict was clean on the criticals (INSERT + UPDATE self-grant both closed) with one LOW folded in (the webhook now accepts any of multiple v1 signatures for key rotation). **Gate:** migration `20260616200000` applies on the next Lovable sync; live charging waits on the founder provisioning the Stripe secrets (`STRIPE_SECRET_KEY`, `STRIPE_PRICE_PRO`, `STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET`). Built file-disjoint from M-A Slice 2. **Files:** `supabase/migrations/20260616200000_mc_plan_tier.sql`, `src/lib/entitlements.ts` (+`.test.ts`), `src/lib/billing.functions.ts`, `src/routes/api/stripe/webhook.ts` new; `src/routes/_authenticated.settings.tsx` (Plan tab + `BillingTab`) edited; `docs/features/pricing.md` (new) + features index, `active-task.md`, this log.

**M-C memory expiry: the "charge for memory persistence" gate is now enforced (BUILT, working tree).** The plan-tier foundation defined the entitlement (`memoryPersists`); this wires the mechanic. Free workspaces keep distilled `agent_memory` for 14 days then it expires; pro and team keep it forever. Implemented entirely additively so it never touched the parallel M-A Slice 2 files (which only added `ExecutedCard.tsx` + `today.functions.ts` + the Today route): a `BEFORE INSERT` trigger (`set_agent_memory_expiry`) stamps `agent_memory.expires_at` from the owner's plan (free = `created_at` + 14 days mirroring `FREE_MEMORY_RETENTION_DAYS`, pro/team = NULL), so the TS write path (`rememberOutcome`) is unchanged and pre-migration tolerant; the `match_agent_memory` recall RPC gains `AND (expires_at IS NULL OR expires_at > now())` so the loop never recalls expired memory (body copied verbatim from the P1 rescope with the one predicate added, security boundary `user_id = COALESCE(auth.uid(), for_user)` preserved); and the daily `memory-tick` cron hard-deletes expired rows (pre-migration tolerant: a missing-column error is ignored, the existing decay passes still run). Existing rows are grandfathered (`expires_at` NULL = never expires) so nothing is retroactively wiped, including the demo seed. **Adversarial review (NEEDS-FIXES, both folded before commit):** (A) a free user could self-grant permanent memory by inserting an explicit far-future `expires_at` (the trigger now only honors a client-supplied value for the service-role; every other caller has it recomputed from the plan, so the value is uncheatable); (B) non-owner team members got FREE expiry (the paid check now keys on `workspace_members` membership, not just `owner_id`, so owners and invited members of any pro/team workspace keep memory). Recall-boundary, trigger-cannot-break-inserts, paid-never-swept, and grandfathering all reviewed clean. **Verification:** `bun test` 117 green, `bun run build` green. **Gate:** migration `20260616210000` applies on the next Lovable sync, after `20260616200000` (plan_tier), in filename order. Built file-disjoint from M-A Slice 2 (which had already landed). **Files:** `supabase/migrations/20260616210000_mc_memory_expiry.sql` new; `src/routes/api/public/hooks/memory-tick.ts` (expiry sweep) edited; `docs/features/pricing.md` (How it works + deferred flipped), `active-task.md`, this log.

**M-C scope ruling: pricing ENGINE only, gates DORMANT at the prototype stage (founder, 2026-06-16).** The founder clarified that at this working-prototype stage we build the pricing engine (plan tiers, entitlements as data, billing surface, Stripe plumbing) but do NOT wire active paywall gates yet, since the product itself is not fully built. So the memory-expiry enforcement shipped just above (the only active gate) is made dormant rather than reverted: a `memory_expiry_enabled()` SQL flag (returns false) gates the stamp trigger, so while off every memory row stays `expires_at = NULL` (never expires) and the recall filter + the `memory-tick` sweep are automatic no-ops. The code is built and reviewed; flip the flag (`CREATE OR REPLACE ... SELECT true`) when ready to enforce. Critic-everywhere and other entitlement gates are explicitly NOT wired now. The entitlements map still documents the intended per-tier policy as pure data (nothing reads it to block). **Files:** `supabase/migrations/20260616210000_mc_memory_expiry.sql` (flag + trigger guard), `docs/features/pricing.md`, `active-task.md`, this log.

**H3 ┬À Scheduling ÔÇö calendar-aware deep-work blocks ÔÇö SHIPPED to `main` (Feature Dashboard pick, claimed before building, adversarially reviewed).** The Calendar surface gains a **"Plan deep work"** action: a new read-only `proposeWorkBlocks` server fn fits the operator's open deep-work tasks (`is_deep_work`, not done) into free time within their working hours, reusing the proven `proposeSlots` conflict logic ÔÇö one block per task, back to back across the next working days, skipping weekends, hours outside the profile's working window, and existing calendar events. It is a pure proposal (never writes); each proposed block has an "Add to calendar" affordance that creates the event via `createCalendarEvent`. **Honest by construction:** it only schedules what genuinely fits, so a packed calendar yields fewer (or zero) blocks with an honest empty state, never a forced plan. **Verification:** `bun run build` green, `bunx eslint` clean; Playwright-verified live both ways ÔÇö the empty state ("Nothing to scheduleÔÇª") on the demo (no open deep-work tasks), and the populated path (temporarily relaxing the deep-work filter, then reverting) produced 6 correct back-to-back hourly blocks (Wed 9amÔÇô2pm) all inside working hours, correctly starting the NEXT working day because it was already past 6pm. **Adversarial review (2-lens workflow, ultracode):** surfaced one real HIGH bug ÔÇö the working-hours boundary used the truncated `getHours()`, so a block from a :30 cursor could overrun `whEnd` by up to the block length (e.g. 17:30ÔåÆ18:30 past a 6pm end); fixed by comparing the block END in minutes in **both** `proposeWorkBlocks` and the pre-existing `proposeSlots` (same one-line bug, same file). Also fixed a MEDIUM: a user-facing em-dash in the empty-state copy (humanized hard gate). A LOW timezone limitation (server-UTC hour checks, shared with `proposeSlots`) was already disclosed in the doc comment and left as a separate platform fix. - **2026-06-15 ┬À M-0 ┬À KI-23 fixed: dispatched specialist runs now resume (the same `model`-column bug, in a SELECT Lovable's insert-only fix missed).** With the hollow-completion fixed, the loop planned and dispatched but the first specialist sat `queued` forever and never executed. Root cause: `resumeAgentLoop` (`loop.server.ts`) selected a `model` column from `agent_runs` that does not exist, so the PostgREST select errored, the run read back null, and the function threw `run not found` on every per-minute `resume-runs` tick ÔÇö so no queued specialist run was ever resumed. Fixed by dropping `model` from both selects; the model now falls back to the checkpoint state then the `google/gemini-2.5-flash` default, exactly as `runAgentLoop` already does. `bun run build` green (3.16s), `bun test` 88 green. **Deploys on the next Lovable Publish, then re-verify a mission hops discovery-scout to strategist to completion end to end.** **Files:** `src/lib/ai/loop.server.ts`, `src/lib/studio.functions.ts`; doc-loop in `docs/planning/{known-issues.md,v7-build-status.md}`, this log.
- **2026-06-15 ┬À M-0 hollow orchestrated missions RESOLVED and verified live; the true cause was a schema-mismatched `agent_runs` insert.** A long multi-layer hunt (approval gating, governance halt, slug drift, deploy divergence) bottomed out on the real blocker: `src/lib/ai/loop.server.ts` inserted a `model:` field into `agent_runs`, a column the table does not have, so the orchestrator's launch INSERT was silently rejected by Postgres (no run row, no trace, no error surfaced) and every orchestrated mission completed hollow or failed at launch. Pinned by exhausting every other lever on the live app (kill-switch off, workspace and roster verified fine, the slug-resolver fix had zero effect), then reading `ai_events` (no `orchestrator:plan` event ever recorded) plus an empty `agent_runs` for a failed mission; Lovable removed `model:` from both insert sites (commit `f1d4e8df41` on `main`). Founder Published; VERIFIED LIVE: mission `973800a8` planned a real 6-step DAG (Strategist, Sprint Planner, Critic, Copilot, Critic, Stakeholder), persisted the steps, and dispatched step 0 with a handoff to the Strategist (cost $0.02, about 90k tokens, trace `bd4f5677`, executed unattended on the auto trust arc). The slug-resolver (`orchestrator.server.ts`) and the loud-fail guard (`maybeCompleteMission` marks a never-planned mission `failed`, not hollow-`completed`) are real hardening and remain, but were secondary. **Two durable findings:** (1) deploys are manual via Lovable Publish ÔÇö both tools commit to `main`, the live app lags `main` until a Publish, and the `lovable-sync-*` branch is a stale artifact, so always verify the deployed build, not just the repo. - **2026-06-15 ┬À `M-0 ┬À orchestrated missions were completing HOLLOW; root-caused live and fixed (the real mission-run blocker)`.** Live re-verification of the prior gating fix on the hosted app (Project GlassWing, demo account) confirmed that fix works (no new control-flow approvals queued) but surfaced a deeper, separate defect: every orchestrated mission finished with 0 steps and 0 hops yet was labeled "completed". A full live trace (`6471cbaa`, 10 hops, 21,183 tokens) proved the cause and ruled out the governance-halt theory (kill-switch off, real tokens spent): the orchestrator's `mission.plan` planner emits a colloquial agent slug (`discovery`), but the seeded roster slug is `discovery-scout` (the same slug drift the 2026-06-14 migration standardized on the event-reactor path), and `mission.plan`'s strict exact-match validator threw on the miss, dropping the WHOLE plan; the orchestrator then observed 0 steps, retried, and finalized "unresolvable internal planning", after which the cron completed the 0-step mission. That is why missions never "hopped". **Fix, two layers:** (1) `mission.plan` (`orchestrator.server.ts`) now resolves each planned slug against the live roster (exact, then a single unambiguous prefix or substring match) so `discovery` maps to `discovery-scout` instead of dropping the plan, throwing clearly only when a slug is genuinely unresolvable; (2) `maybeCompleteMission` (`handoff.server.ts`) now marks a never-planned (0-step) terminal mission `failed` (retryable) instead of hollow-`completed`, and skips decision-capture for it, so any future zero-plan cause surfaces loudly rather than as a fake "done". **Verification:** `bun run build` green, `bun test` 88 green. **Live re-verification pending the next Lovable deploy** (the fix cannot be observed on the hosted app until it deploys). **Infra note:** confirmed with the founder we keep ONE Lovable-managed Supabase (no new account, no DB fork); schema continues to flow through `supabase/migrations/*` applied by Lovable. **Files:** `src/lib/ai/tools/orchestrator.server.ts`, `src/lib/ai/handoff.server.ts`; `docs/planning/{known-issues.md,v7-build-status.md}`, `active-task.md`, this log.

- **2026-06-14 ┬À `M-0 ┬À orchestrator control-flow tools no longer approval-gated (the live mission-stall fix)`.** Live end-to-end verification on the hosted app (the M-0 exit gate) surfaced the real blocker, which neither the migration sync nor code review had: a freshly launched orchestrated mission stalled. Root-caused via a recon workflow plus a live server-fn response-trace capture (Playwright): the orchestrator's OWN control-flow tools (`mission.plan`, `mission.dispatch`) were being sent to the approval queue at the `observing` arc (`resolveApprovalMode` forces auto to review there), so the plan never persisted; the orchestrator then observed zero steps and finalized with "mission steps are not being registered". The 7 stuck Today approvals were exactly these expired queued plan/dispatch calls. Founder ruling: orchestration control-flow tools always run inline. **Fix:** a new `ORCHESTRATION_CONTROL_FLOW_TOOLS` allowlist (`mission.plan/dispatch/observe/finalize`) at the single loop gate (`loop.server.ts:647-665`) bypasses approval creation for those four (no external side effect; `mission.dispatch` only enqueues child runs; the specialists' real-world tools stay gated per arc on the child runs; kill-switch/budget/guardrails still apply because they live in `callModel` upstream of the gate). **Plus three defense-in-depth guards** (the RCA + its adversarial verifier showed a completion-guard alone was insufficient and could strand a mission): the `agent_runs` insert now throws on error (no silent 0-run loop); `startOrchestratedMission` marks the mission `halted` on a thrown launch before re-throwing (so the UI retry, gated on failed/halted, fires instead of leaving it `running`); and `maybeCompleteMission` no longer silently completes a zero-step mission unless a terminal orchestrator run exists (closing the hollow-completion the RCA found, without stranding, since a failed launch now goes to `halted`). **Verification:** `bun run build` green, `bun test` 88 green, adversarial review safe-to-land (allowlist exact, governance not bypassed, no mission stranding); diff scrutinized at the gate. **Live re-verification pending the Lovable deploy of this commit** (the fix cannot be observed on the hosted app until it deploys). **Files:** `src/lib/ai/{loop.server,trust.server,handoff.server}.ts`, `src/lib/orchestrator.functions.ts`; this log + `active-task.md`.

- **2026-06-14 ┬À `M-0 #4 ┬À humanizeText() runtime sanitizer`.** The hard gate from the humanized-output convention (Level 2) is now wired at the AI chokepoint, so the platform's generated prose carries no machine fingerprints. New pure `src/lib/ai/humanize.ts` (`humanizeText`) segments prose from fenced and inline code, normalizes em/en dashes to honest ASCII by context (a numeric range like 1-6 becomes "1 to 6"; a separator dash becomes a comma), strips the convention's invisible and exotic-space set, collapses double spaces, trims trailing whitespace; its own source spells the code points as escapes so it stays fingerprint-free and lint-clean. Wired into `runtime.server.ts`: `callModel` humanizes prose output, `callModelStream` humanizes on a line-buffered, fence-aware boundary (`createStreamHumanizer` holds an open fenced block until it closes, so streamed concatenation equals `humanizeText(whole)`), plus a soft `HUMANIZE_DIRECTIVE` on prose system prompts (`prompts.server.ts`). JSON is never touched: every gate keys on `responseFormat !== 'json_object'` and `callModel` parses JSON off the raw text, so the agent loop and all tool JSON stay byte-exact. The per-lane adversarial reviewer ran 164 probe assertions (streaming-equals-whole-text, prefix stability, purity, idempotence, JSON parse-safety) and caught one real gap: `lineage.functions.ts` (PRD to task-graph) returned `{"tasks":[...]}` without declaring json-mode, so the sanitizer would have rewritten task-title strings; fixed by adding `responseFormat: 'json_object'`. The eval-runner subject call is intentionally left humanized (its output is scored as a string, never parsed, so evaluating the shipped form is correct). **Verification:** `bun run build` green, `bun test` 88 green (+27 humanize cases), eslint clean on all touched files. Takes effect on deploy (no migration). **Files:** `src/lib/ai/humanize.ts` (+`.test.ts`) new; `src/lib/ai/{runtime.server,prompts.server}.ts`, `src/lib/lineage.functions.ts` edited; `docs/conventions/humanized-output.md`, `docs/planning/v7-build-status.md`, `active-task.md`, this log.
- **2026-06-14 ┬À `M-0 ┬À KI-19 enabled-agent dispatch hole closed`.** A latent gap the slug-drift RCA surfaced: `resolveAgent` (`handoff.server.ts`) resolved a target agent by slug with no `enabled` filter, so a disabled or off-roster agent could still be dispatched a child run (via the `agent.handoff` tool or the mission dispatcher, which both route through that one chokepoint). Fixed at the chokepoint: `resolveAgent` now filters `enabled = true` and throws a clear, slug-named error (`Target agent 'X' is disabled or not in the roster`) when nothing enabled matches. The throw is caught per step, by `failOrRequeueStep` on the dispatcher path and by the agent loop on the tool path, so a bad target terminalizes one step instead of crashing a run; the orchestrator sender lookup keeps its null-sender fallback, so enabled specialists are unaffected. `agents.enabled` is `BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT true`, so the filter has no null footgun. Adversarial review verdict safe-to-land, no code edits needed. **Residual (logged as KI-20):** two adjacent surfaces still resolve agents without an enabled filter, the run-start path in `loop.server.ts` (an already-queued run whose target was disabled in the gap) and the operator-initiated `runAgent` direct invocation. **Verification:** `bun run build` green, `bun test` 88 green, eslint clean. Takes effect on deploy (no migration). **Files:** `src/lib/ai/handoff.server.ts`, `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts`; `docs/planning/known-issues.md` (KI-19 resolved, KI-20 added), this log.
- **2026-06-14 ┬À `M-0 ┬À unseeded-slug drift sealed (doc-loop + RCA correction)`.** The migration shipped in `5b0b0b93ea`; this entry completes its doc loop and corrects the record. The tracker had claimed the orchestrator prompt's stale slugs made `mission.plan` throw and kill any sensing-step mission. A 10-agent adversarial root-cause (workflow `wf_71a7dc78`: 6 readers, a synthesizer, 3 refuters) disproved it: `mission.plan` plans against the live enabled roster and re-validates (`orchestrator.server.ts:125,173-179`), so it never deterministically throws. The real deterministic defect was on the event-reactor path: `seed_default_event_subscriptions` seeded `signal.created` to slug `'discovery'`, but the roster slug is `discovery-scout`, so `dispatchEvent` (`reactor.functions.ts:222`) threw "Target agent not found" for every new account, killing the autonomous `signal.created` SENSE fan-out (fault-isolated, the `event_queue` row just marks failed, which is why it stayed silent). - **2026-06-14 ÔÇö `v6 Phase 3 ┬À viral loop` ÔÇö shareable decision links: a PM can make a decision public and share it at `/d/<slug>`; the app's first anonymous-read surface, hardened at the DB wire.** ┬º7 growth loop. `decisions` gains `share_slug` (CSPRNG `gen_random_uuid` 32-hex) + `is_public` (default false); a new public route `src/routes/d.$slug.tsx` (SSR loader + dynamic `head()` OG tags ÔÇö the app's first per-route meta) renders a read-only "Made with Cadence" page from `getPublicDecision` (a safe minimal projection: title/rationale/status/who/date, NO joins). - **2026-06-14 ÔÇö `v6 Phase 3 ┬À KI-14` ÔÇö the suite-eval score scale is now honest: standardized on 0ÔÇô100, killing a silent column overflow + a false "below gate" read.** `eval_runs.avg_score` / `eval_case_results.score` were `numeric(4,3)` (max 9.999 ÔÇö a 0ÔÇô1 design), but the live judge (`eval-runner.server.ts`) writes 0ÔÇô100 and `eval_suites.pass_threshold` is INTEGER 0ÔÇô100: a real run ÔëÑ 10 OVERFLOWED the column, and the 0ÔÇô1 demo seeds rendered "score 1 ┬À below gate 80" (a false failure on the screen-7 eval drill). Fix (migration `20260614160000`, no app-logic change): widen both columns ÔåÆ `numeric(6,3)` (holds 0ÔÇô100, keeps the 3-decimal scale so the widen is precision-lossless) + rescale existing 0ÔÇô1 rows ├ù100 across **three** persisted copies ÔÇö `eval_runs`, `eval_case_results`, and the derived `drift_snapshots.avg_eval_score` (drift materializes the same metric at rollup). **Why no app code:** verified against source that `trust.server.ts` reads a DIFFERENT table (`ai_evals.score`, the per-message chat-judge system, still 0ÔÇô1) and `drift.server.ts` feeds the score only through a scale-invariant pct-delta ÔÇö so the recon agents' "trust wraps / drift breaks" alarms were both false (lesson: verify recon against source before editing). - **2026-06-14 ÔÇö `v6 Phase 3 ┬À slice 1 / Track 2` ÔÇö the Gauntlet: the three north-star proof metrics, instrumented on a real surface (honest empty states), built in a parallel worktree then hardened by a 12-finding adversarial review before landing.** New `/govern?tab=gauntlet` tab (inserted after Analytics) with three cards, each a real computation over owner-scoped tables ÔÇö no fabricated numbers; sparse windows read "not enough data yet." **A ┬À Acceptance rate** (`getAcceptanceRate`): `accepted/(accepted+rejected)` over DECIDED rows (`decided_at` set) where accepted = status Ôêê {approved, executed, failed} ÔÇö an approved call that then ran (resolveApprovalÔåÆexecuteApproval flips approvedÔåÆexecuted/failed) is still an acceptance, so the worktree agent's first cut (count only `status='approved'`) read artificially low; review caught it, fixed at the DB layer + in the 7d-vs-prior-7d trend. The user rollup of the per-agent acceptance already in `ai/trust.server.ts`. **C ┬À Autonomy ratio** (`getAutonomyRatio`): `unattended/(unattended+gated)` where unattended = SUCCESSFUL (`ok=true`) side-effecting `tool_calls` rows (a failed inline attempt isn't carried work ÔÇö review fix) and gated = side-effecting `agent_approvals` rows, side-effecting decided by `isSideEffectingTool()` (`tool-consequences.ts`); copy is explicit that rising Ôëá no-human (the gated count is exactly the work that still comes to you). **B ┬À Ritual retention** (`getRitualRetention`): distinct days-active 7/14/30 + current streak from the new `ritual_sessions` table, plus an on-the-fly, user-wide real-vs-demo signal (ÔëÑ1 connected `connections` row OR ÔëÑ1 `signals` row) that returns null (the tag is omitted) if its probe errors, rather than mislabeling a real account "demo" (review fix). **Pre-migration-tolerant:** the `ritual_sessions` read catches a missing-relation error (`42P01`/`42703`/`PGRST205`/"relation does not exist") and returns `tableReady:false` ÔåÆ card reads "not enough data yet" rather than throwing (same probe idiom as `mission-advance.server.ts:hasRetryColumns`). Today (`_authenticated.index.tsx`) fires `recordRitualSession` once on mount (ref-guarded) ÔÇö never blocks render, swallows table-missing/any failure; the write is an idempotent per-UTC-day upsert (unique `(user_id, opened_on)`) so repeated opens never accumulate, and `workspace_id` is left null (a client id isn't trusted ÔÇö cross-tenant; all three review fixes). - **2026-06-14 ÔÇö `v6 Phase 2 ┬À W2 + W3` ÔÇö autonomy made legible: the loop's unattended work is audited, the A2A contract is hardened, and the moat is on the cockpit.** Grounded by two parallel Explore sweeps (which caught that the `/swarm` Swarm HUD already IS the "agents at work" OS view ÔÇö so we enriched it instead of building a redundant `/system` route). **W2 ÔÇö "Executed unattended" audit:** the trust arc already executes write tools inline at trusted/ambient; this surfaces it honestly. `getMission` now flags each `HopToolCall.is_unattended` via the new client-safe `isSideEffectingTool()` (`src/lib/tool-consequences.ts`), and `/missions/$id` renders an "Executed unattended" card (between the gate ÔÇö _what needs you_ ÔÇö and the trace ÔÇö _what already ran_), each row showing the tool's catalogued effect + reversibility + ok/latency. **Correctness crux (verified by review):** every `tool_calls` row is an inline auto-execution ÔÇö gated tools queue an `agent_approvals` row and `executeApproval` updates the approval, never writing `tool_calls` ÔÇö so a side-effecting `tool_calls` row is _provably_ unattended (claim-never-outruns-wiring holds). **W3 ÔÇö A2A hardening + moat visibility:** (a) `enqueueHandoff` (`handoff.server.ts`) now validates `payload.memory_refs[]` against real `agent_memory` ids the user owns, dropping phantom refs before they reach a receiver's prompt (best-effort: a transient query error keeps refs as-is, never strips valid ones; works under both the user client and the admin sweeper). - **2026-06-14 ÔÇö `v6 Phase 2 ┬À W1` ÔÇö the memory moat is real: recorded outcomes now become memory the agents recall.** Phase 2's first demoable unit (the Decision-System moat, v6 ┬º3 Pillar 2), grounded by an Explore sweep that found the loop was only _half_-wired: `recordOutcome` re-scored the opportunity ICE and wrote a `learnings` audit row, but that row lived in a table **no agent ever reads** ÔÇö `match_agent_memory` (the loop's recall) only reads `agent_memory`. So the product _showed_ "we learned this" while every agent stayed amnesiac (claim-outruns-wiring). Fix: on `recordOutcome`, after the learning insert, distil the outcome into a **global-scope, embedded `agent_memory` row** (`src/lib/ai/outcome-memory.ts` pure `buildOutcomeMemory`/`outcomeImportance` + `src/lib/ai/memory.server.ts` `rememberOutcome`), entity-linked in `metadata` to the prd/opportunity/learning. Because the row is `scope='global'`, `match_agent_memory`'s `m.scope='global'` clause returns it to a future run of **any** agent (when semantically relevant), and Phase 1's `memory_refs[]` threading carries it across hops ÔÇö so a Strategist re-encountering the opportunity now recalls "we shipped this; it was {verdict} (ICE {prior}ÔåÆ{new})." Importance 4 (decisive) / 3 (mixed) keeps it above the memory-tick decay floor. **Adversarial review (1 agent) found 4 real issues, all fixed:** (1) a null-embedding row is silently _unrecallable_ (the RPC hard-filters `embedding IS NOT NULL`) and there's no re-embed sweep ÔåÆ now we **skip the write entirely** rather than insert a ghost (also closes an `embedOne` sparse-return path); (2) the idempotency delete used `.eq("metadata->>source",ÔÇª)` ÔÇö the repo's proven jsonb idiom is `.filter("col->>key","eq",ÔÇª)` (per `today.functions.ts`/`traces.functions.ts`) ÔåÆ switched, so re-records replace not duplicate; (3) a clamped-confidence outcome could render a misleading "8.3ÔåÆ8.3" ICE move ÔåÆ the move line now guards on the _rounded_ values; (4) RLS/blast-radius confirmed safe (`recordOutcome`'s extra `memory_id` return field is ignored by `OutcomeCard`). **Verification:** `bun test` 23 green (9 new pure-policy tests incl. the rounding-honesty case), `bun run build` green, touched files prettier/eslint-clean. No new UI: the recall surfaces in any run's "Relevant memories from past sessions" prompt block + trace (and the existing Memory panel still shows the `learnings` audit). **Files:** `src/lib/ai/outcome-memory.ts` (+`.test.ts`) new; `src/lib/ai/memory.server.ts` (+`rememberOutcome`), `src/lib/outcome.functions.ts` (distil hook + title selects) edited; `architecture/orchestration.md`, `docs/strategy/session-decisions.md`, `active-task.md`, this log.

- **2026-06-14 ÔÇö `v6 Phase 1 (The Loop Runs Itself)` COMPLETE: autonomy, wired ÔÇö a multi-hop mission now runs unattended, retries transient hop failures, sizes its own step budget, and threads compounding memory across hops.** Closes the four gaps the runtime audit named (v6 Appendix B) ÔÇö _not_ with messaging, with code. Founder design rulings this session (AskUserQuestion, logged in session-decisions): auto-advance folds into the existing `resume-runs` sweeper (no new pg*cron ÔåÆ no migration-apply gate); hop retry is bounded (2 attempts + exponential backoff); the step budget is arc + mission-size aware. **(1) Deterministic auto-advance** ÔÇö new `src/lib/ai/mission-advance.server.ts` (`advanceMissionCore`): reflect child-run outcomes onto `mission_steps` ÔåÆ dispatch every newly-ready step ÔåÆ finalize a terminal DAG, all **model-free**. Key insight: the old `advanceMission` re-invoked the orchestrator \_LLM* each wave, but `mission.plan` already rejects re-planning, so that call only ever did mechanical observeÔåÆdispatchÔåÆfinalize ÔÇö replacing it with deterministic DB ops is cheaper, faster, and concurrency-safe while preserving behavior (the LLM now runs only for the initial plan). The per-minute `resume-runs` cron calls it for every running mission; the manual `advanceMission` server fn calls the same core; `mission.dispatch` (the orchestrator tool) routes through the shared `dispatchReadySteps`. **Claim-first CAS** (`plannedÔåÆdispatched` before enqueue) makes overlapping ticks safe from double-dispatch; a step stranded `dispatched` with null `run_id` (worker eviction mid-enqueue) is recovered after a 3-min window. **(2) Bounded hop retry** ÔÇö migration `20260614090000` adds `mission_steps.{attempts,max_attempts,next_retry_at}` and teaches `next_ready_mission_steps` the backoff window (identical signature, backward-compatible: NULL backoff = eligible now); pure policy in `src/lib/ai/retry.ts`. Pre-migration-tolerant via a per-isolate `hasRetryColumns` probe that only caches a genuine missing-column error (a transient blip re-probes), degrading to no-retry without ever throwing. **(3) Adaptive step budget** ÔÇö new `src/lib/ai/budget.ts` (`adaptiveStepBudget`) replaces the static `maxStepsFor`: role base + earned-trust headroom (`arc`) + orchestrator-scales-with-DAG-size, under a hard ceiling; orchestrator base kept at the proven 14 so the initial run never regresses (review catch). Threaded through `executeLoop` (both `runAgentLoop` + `resumeAgentLoop`) with a live `mission_steps` count. **(4) `memory_refs[]` populated** (the W5 contract field) ÔÇö new `src/lib/ai/memory.server.ts` (`recallMemoryRefs`) returns the `id`s the RPC already exposed; the loop's recall now writes `agent_memory.last_used_at` on every recall (decay input), and each dispatched hop threads relevant memory into the handoff payload. Migration `20260614091000` rescopes `match_agent_memory` to `COALESCE(auth.uid(), for_user)` so the **service-role sweeper path** actually matches semantic memory (was `auth.uid()`-only ÔåÆ null on the autonomous path ÔÇö the exact claim-outruns-wiring gap Phase 1 exists to close) while keeping the per-user security boundary (auth.uid() always wins). **Verification:** new `bun test` path (bun's built-in runner ÔÇö zero new deps, dodges the supply-chain guard) covers the pure budget/retry policy (14 tests green); `bun run build` green; touched files prettier/eslint-clean; a 2-agent adversarial review over the diff surfaced 10 findings ÔÇö 4 real (orchestrator budget regression, transient-error caching, stranded-dispatch recovery, the `match_agent_memory` `auth.uid()` gap), all fixed; 3 confidently wrong (verified against source ÔÇö one proposed "fix" would have introduced an infinite retry loop), rejected. **Gate (unchanged pattern):** the two P1 migrations apply on the next Lovable sync; until then retry is off and autonomous-path `memory_refs` carries reflections only ÔÇö both degrade gracefully. **Files:** `src/lib/ai/{mission-advance.server,memory.server,budget,retry}.ts` (+ `budget.test.ts`/`retry.test.ts`) new; `src/lib/ai/{loop.server,handoff.server}.ts`, `src/lib/ai/tools/orchestrator.server.ts`, `src/lib/orchestrator.functions.ts`, `src/routes/api/public/hooks/resume-runs.ts` edited; `supabase/migrations/{20260614090000_p1_mission_step_retry,20260614091000_p1_memory_recall_for_user}.sql` new; `package.json`/`tsconfig.json` (test path); `architecture/orchestration.md`, `docs/features/{loop-runs-itself.md(new),README.md}`, `docs/planning/known-issues.md`, `docs/strategy/session-decisions.md`, `active-task.md`, this log.

- **2026-06-06 ÔÇö Calendar Parts B + C shipped (pending provider Client IDs).** Per-user calendar OAuth (`F-CALENDAR-PERUSER`): new table `public.user_calendar_connections` (RLS-scoped to `auth.uid()`); canonical app-user OAuth helpers landed at `src/integrations/lovable/appUserConnector.ts` (server-only) + `appUserConnectorClient.ts` (popup-driver, browser-safe); new `src/lib/calendar-connections.functions.ts` (`startCalendarConnect` ┬À `saveCalendarConnection` ┬À `listMyCalendarConnections` ┬À `disconnectCalendar` ┬À `getPrimaryConnection`); `src/lib/calendar.functions.ts` `syncCalendar` / `createCalendarEvent` / `updateCalendarEvent` / `deleteCalendarEvent` are now provider-aware ÔÇö Google ÔåÆ `google_calendar` connector path, Microsoft ÔåÆ `microsoft_outlook` (Graph) via `callAsAppUser`, and the existing workspace connector stays as fallback when the user has no per-user connection. - **2026-06-06 ÔÇö Bundle 9 Slices 2 + 3 shipped ÔÇö Builder now closes its own CI loop and runs safely in parallel. FND-RUNTIME 0.9 forced-restart playbook published.** **Slice 2 (CI loop):** two new built-in tools ÔÇö `github.ci.read` (`read`/`auto`: `GET /pulls/{n}` ÔåÆ head sha ÔåÆ `GET /commits/{sha}/check-runs` + `/status`; returns `{overall: pending|success|failure|neutral, checks[], head_sha, ÔÇª}`; cached via `withIdempotency('github_ci', '<pr>-<head_sha>', ÔÇª)` so re-polls don't burn quota and the cache invalidates naturally when the branch's head_sha moves) and `github.commit.append` (`write`/`confirm`: PUTs a single new file on the PR's head branch via Contents API; same `.github/` / `supabase/migrations/` / `.env` / lockfile deny-list as `github.pr.open`; wrapped in `withIdempotency('github_commit', a.idempotency_key, ÔÇª)` keyed by `issue-<n>-fix-<k>`). The Builder system prompt now mandates: after `github.pr.open`, call `github.ci.read` up to 3├ù per loop step; on `success`/`neutral` finalize; on `pending` finalize with a wait note and let `resume-runs` re-enter; on `failure` propose ONE follow-up `github.commit.append` whose message names the failing check, then finalize. `listBuilderRuns()` extended to surface the latest `github.ci.read` result per run and expose `failing.{name,html_url,summary}` so the `/build` card and `/missions/$id` timeline render a `CI ┬À green | red ┬À <check> | pending | n/a` chip that links to the failing check. **Slice 3 (conflict guard):** new `builder_file_claims` table ÔÇö `(user_id, workspace_id, run_id, mission_id, mission_title, repo, path, status, claimed_at, released_at, released_reason)` with a **partial unique index `(repo, path) WHERE status='held'`** so only one held claim per `(repo, path)` exists at a time; RLS = workspace members read, owner writes; PostgREST grants in the same migration. `github.pr.open` now INSERTs the claim row BEFORE the Contents-API PUT and surfaces a typed `BuilderFileConflict: path "<p>" is already claimed by another Builder mission ("<title>")` error on the unique violation ÔÇö second-mission PR never opens, no branch is created. New SECURITY DEFINER trigger `release_claims_for_terminal_run` (`AFTER UPDATE OF status ON agent_runs`) auto-releases every `held` claim for a run that hits `completed | completed_with_failures | halted | failed`. Operator can force-release via the new **Active file claims** panel on `/build` (5s refresh) which calls new server fn `releaseBuilderClaim({claim_id})` ÔÇö the Release button is only enabled for the claim owner. **FND-RUNTIME 0.9 playbook:** new `docs/operations/fnd-runtime-restart-playbook.md` is the operator-driven verification ÔÇö start a Builder mission, restart the worker mid-loop, verify the resume-runs sweeper picks the run up within Ôëñ60s, every idempotency-keyed external write (`github_pr`, `github_commit`, `github_ci`) returns its cached result, repo state matches the single-mission contract (one branch, one PR, one initial commit, optionally one fix commit). `docs/planning/foundation-audit.md` row 0.9 flipped ÔØî ÔåÆ ­ƒƒí with a pointer to the playbook (Ô£à on a clean pass). **Docs loop closed in the same commit:** new `docs/features/bundle-9-builder.md` (canonical per-feature page covering Slice 1 + 2 + 3 ÔÇö demo script, verification per slice, tool contracts, governance, known limits), new `docs/operations/fnd-runtime-restart-playbook.md`, both indexed in `docs/README.md` + `docs/features/README.md`; `architecture/orchestration.md` Bundle 9 paragraph extended with the new tools + claims ledger. **WHY:** Slice 1 proved the PlanÔåÆBuild hop end-to-end against a real repo but left two open gaps that block claim C2 ("one governed loop") at production volume ÔÇö (a) the Builder couldn't see whether its own PR passed CI, so the operator was still the test pipeline, and (b) two parallel missions could silently race on the same file, breaking the autonomy story the moment more than one PRD hit Builder. With Slices 2 + 3 in place the Builder closes its own loop on red and the conflict guard makes parallel Builder dispatch safe ÔÇö both are prerequisites for an operator-trustable autonomous build lane. **Out of scope this turn (queued):** `github.ci.logs` tool (Builder still only sees check name + summary, not raw job log), `github.pr.update` / `github.pr.merge` (operator owns merge), per-workspace `GITHUB_REPO` (still a single global secret), Restructure Phases 3ÔÇô4 (theme polish; operator deferred until feature tweaks settle), Proof Platform bundles 10ÔÇô12 (Ship ┬À Launch ┬À SupportÔåÆLearn). **Gotchas:** (1) the claim is held by `run_id`, so a single mission re-running `github.pr.open` (e.g. via the idempotency cache path) skips the conflict branch because the holder check matches `existing.run_id === runId`. (2) The CI cache key is `<pr>-<head_sha>`, so after `github.commit.append` lands a new commit the next `github.ci.read` call sees a new head_sha and bypasses the cache ÔÇö exactly what we want. (3) The auto-release trigger keys off `OLD.status IS DISTINCT FROM NEW.status` so a no-op UPDATE on a terminal run won't try to release already-released rows. (4) `releaseBuilderClaim` is RLS-scoped to the claim's `user_id` ÔÇö workspace peers can SEE the claim but cannot release each other's; this is intentional until we add a workspace-admin role. **Files:** new `supabase/migrations/<ts>_builder_ci_loop_tools.sql` (Builder prompt + 2 new tool seeds + backfill), new `supabase/migrations/<ts>_builder_file_claims.sql` (claims table + index + grants + RLS + auto-release trigger), new `docs/features/bundle-9-builder.md`, new `docs/operations/fnd-runtime-restart-playbook.md`; edited `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts` (two new tools + claim acquire in `github.pr.open`), `src/lib/build.functions.ts` (CI surface in `listBuilderRuns`, new `listBuilderClaims` + `releaseBuilderClaim`), `src/routes/_authenticated.build.tsx` (CI chip + active-claims panel), `docs/README.md`, `docs/features/README.md`, `docs/planning/foundation-audit.md`, `docs/planning/feature-backlog.md`, `architecture/orchestration.md`, `plan.md`.

- **2026-06-06 ÔÇö F-AGENT-4: Swarm HUD + per-feature demo/operator docs pattern.** Closes the agent-ecosystem bundle. New route `/swarm` (nav slot: Agents ÔåÆ Swarm HUD, between Missions and Prompt Studio) is a single read-only governor's cockpit over the existing substrate ÔÇö no new tables, no new tools, no new mutations. One server fn `getSwarmHud()` in `src/lib/swarm.functions.ts` parallel-fires every read (RLS-scoped to `auth.uid()` + workspace via `current_user_default_workspace`): agents + latest non-terminal `agent_runs` per agent (priority `running > paused > queued > terminal`) joined to `agent_autonomy.arc`; missions filtered to `planning|running|completed_with_failures` OR `completed_at >= now()-1h` with `mission_steps` `done/total/failed` aggregates; last 50 `agent_messages` for the handoff feed; pending `agent_approvals`; last 50 `event_queue` rows; throughput from `ai_events` last 60 min bucketed in JS into 5-min windows (count, sum `est_cost_usd`, p50 `latency_ms`); `guardrail_hits` count for the same hour. The page (`src/routes/_authenticated.swarm.tsx`) refreshes every 2s via TanStack Query (`refetchIntervalInBackground: false`), composes 7 inline section components, and has error + not-found boundaries. Writes are zero net-new: inline Approve/Reject calls `resolveApproval` from `governance.functions.ts`; Dispatch/Skip on pending `confirm` reactor rows calls `decideEventDispatch` from `reactor.functions.ts`. **Docs pattern alongside the build:** new `docs/features/` folder with one canonical operator/demo page per shipped feature ÔÇö `docs/features/README.md` (index + template), `f-agent-1-orchestrator.md`, `f-agent-2-memory-reflection.md`, `f-agent-3-event-reactor.md` (backfilled, ~80 lines each, consolidated from the existing plan ┬º4 entries + architecture bullets ÔÇö no new claims), and `f-agent-4-swarm-hud.md` (full). Each follows the same skeleton: What it does ┬À Why ┬À Where to find ┬À Demo script Ôëñ 90s ┬À How it works ┬À Governance & guardrails ┬À Verification checklist ┬À Limits ┬À Related. `docs/README.md` got a new "Per-feature operator & demo guides" section linking the four pages. **WHY:** F-AGENT-1 made Cadence plan, F-AGENT-2 made it learn, F-AGENT-3 made it react ÔÇö together they produce more concurrent activity than the operator can track from four separate surfaces (`/missions`, `/inbox`, `/agents`, `/governance`). The HUD makes governance scale with the swarm. The features folder makes every shipped capability demo-ready and onboardable from one page, so future demos, sales calls, and onboarding don't have to grep ┬º4 entries + architecture bullets to reconstruct what a feature actually does. **Out of scope (deferred):** pause/steer-from-graph controls, `agent.spawn` fan-out + parent merge (E4 polish), per-mission message-cap loop guard, cross-workspace HUD, retro-priced cost re-calculation, numeric `trust_score` column on `agent_autonomy` (only the arc is shown), and any new mutations beyond the four reused buttons. **Gotchas:** (1) `agent_autonomy` does not have a `trust_score` column ÔÇö only `arc`. (2) `getSwarmHud` returns jsonb blobs typed as `any` to satisfy TanStack Start's serialization checker. (3) Latest-run-per-agent is computed in JS (not SQL) so we can apply the `running > paused > queued > terminal` priority ÔÇö an 80-row query window is sufficient for an active swarm. (4) No new index ships with this; if `getSwarmHud()` p50 climbs above ~200ms on a large workspace, add covering indexes on `agent_messages(created_at desc)` and `event_queue(created_at desc)` in a small follow-on migration. **Files:** new `src/lib/swarm.functions.ts`, new `src/routes/_authenticated.swarm.tsx`, new `docs/features/README.md` + 4 feature pages; edited `src/components/cadence/AppShell.tsx` (Swarm HUD nav item), `docs/README.md`, `architecture/orchestration.md`, `docs/planning/feature-backlog.md`, `plan.md`.

- **2026-06-06 ÔÇö F-AGENT-3: Event reactor + auto-pipelines.** Closes the last "agents do, not just react when summoned" gap. Two new tables: `event_subscriptions` (per-workspace rules: `event_type Ôêê {signal.created, opportunity.scored, prd.approved} ÔåÆ target_agent_slug` with `approval_mode auto|confirm` and jsonb `filter`; RLS workspace-member read + owner write, `is_default` flag distinguishes seeded vs operator rules) and `event_queue` (one row per firing, idempotent UNIQUE `(subscription_id, source_id)` so re-firing triggers is a no-op; statuses `pending ÔåÆ dispatched | skipped | failed`; carries `mission_id`/`run_id`/`error`). Three SECURITY DEFINER trigger fns fan-out matching subs into the queue: `signals` (AFTER INSERT), `opportunities` (only on insert or ICE-input change AND `NEW.ice_score >= COALESCE(filter->>'min_score', 8.0)`), `prds` (only on transition into `status='approved'`). New `seed_default_event_subscriptions(uuid)` seeds three defaults per workspace owner ÔÇö `signal.created ÔåÆ discovery (auto)`, `opportunity.scored ÔåÆ strategist (confirm, min_score 8.0)`, `prd.approved ÔåÆ orchestrator (confirm)`; wired into `handle_new_user` for new signups and backfilled for every existing workspace owner. New `src/lib/reactor.functions.ts` exposes `listEventSubscriptions`, `upsertEventSubscription` (verifies the target agent exists for the user before saving), `deleteEventSubscription`, `listEventQueue`, `decideEventDispatch` (operator approve/reject for `confirm` rows), and a shared `dispatchEvent()` helper that creates a real mission via `createMission` + runs `runAgentLoop` with a templated, event-type-specific goal. New cron route `/api/public/hooks/event-reactor-tick` drains pending `auto`-mode rows (BATCH=10) every minute via pg_cron job `event-reactor-tick`. `confirm`-mode rows stay pending until the operator clicks Dispatch/Skip on the new **Reactor activity** panel on `/governance` (5s auto-refresh). `/governance` also gained an **Auto-pipelines** panel: rule list with enable/disable/delete + add-rule composer (event type / agent slug / mode / min-ICE filter). **WHY:** F-AGENT-1 gave Cadence a planner, F-AGENT-2 gave it memory + autonomy; without a reactor the system still required an operator to push every button. With the reactor in place, a high-ICE opportunity auto-queues a PRD-draft mission, an approved PRD queues an orchestrator plan, and a fresh signal auto-clusters ÔÇö the discoverÔåÆdefineÔåÆplan chain runs itself end-to-end behind governance gates. **Out of scope (queued):** F-AGENT-4 (Swarm HUD). **Gotchas:** (1) The dispatch helper calls `runAgentLoop` synchronously inside the cron handler ÔÇö fine for `auto` orchestrator rows because backpressure already enqueues over-cap missions, but high-frequency event types should wrap with `withIdempotency` or move behind a true queue. (2) Opportunity trigger only checks `>=` against `filter->>'min_score'` (default 8.0); no other comparators yet. (3) Trigger functions are SECURITY DEFINER because the inserting role may not have direct INSERT on `event_queue` ÔÇö do NOT switch to SECURITY INVOKER. (4) Defaults use `is_default=true` so a future "reset" button can re-seed without clobbering operator rules. **Files:** new `supabase/migrations/<ts>_event_reactor_and_subscriptions.sql`, new `src/lib/reactor.functions.ts`, new `src/routes/api/public/hooks/event-reactor-tick.ts`; edited `src/routes/_authenticated.governance.tsx`, `docs/planning/feature-backlog.md`, `architecture/orchestration.md`, `plan.md`.
- **2026-06-06 ÔÇö F-AGENT-1: Orchestrator + multi-agent mission decomposition.** First half of the "agent ecosystem" bundle. The substrate (chokepoint, agent*runs, agent_messages, checkpoints, trust, guardrails, missions) already existed but every mission was effectively single-agent ÔÇö `agent.handoff` was a primitive without a meta-planner. New seed agent `orchestrator` (created on first use via `seed_orchestrator_agent(p_user_id)` SECURITY DEFINER fn; idempotent re-seed bumps the system-prompt + tool wiring). New `mission_steps` table: `(mission_id, idx, agent_slug, sub_goal, depends_on int[], status, run_id, message_id, result, error, rationale, dispatched_at, completed_at)`; RLS scoped to `auth.uid()=user_id` with workspace_member read; unique on `(mission_id, idx)`. New SQL helper `next_ready_mission_steps(mission_id)` returns step rows whose `depends_on` are all `status='done'`. Four new agent tools registered: `mission.plan` calls a sub-model with a planning system prompt (lists the user's actual specialist roster, asks for strict JSON `{summary, steps:[{agent_slug, sub_goal, depends_on, rationale}]}`, 1ÔÇô8 steps cap, validates every slug is real before persisting); `mission.dispatch` reflects in-flight child-run statuses, then for every ready step calls `enqueueHandoff()` (existing primitive) to insert a child `agent_runs` row + `agent_messages` row, marks the step `dispatched`, records `run_id` + `message_id`; `mission.observe` reflects + returns per-step state + a status histogram + `all_terminal` boolean; `mission.finalize` requires `all_terminal`, marks the mission `completed` or `completed_with_failures`. Loop step cap is per-agent now via `maxStepsFor(agentSlug)` ÔÇö orchestrator gets 14 to fit plan + observe/dispatch cycles + finalize; specialists keep 6. Three new server fns in `src/lib/orchestrator.functions.ts`: `ensureOrchestrator()` for explicit bootstrap, `startOrchestratedMission({goal,title?,model?})` for the canonical entry (idempotent seed + roster pre-flight + mission row + orchestrator loop), `advanceMission({missionId})` for the operator to push the next round of dispatches manually until F-AGENT-3 wires automatic re-wake, plus `listMissionSteps({missionId})` for read. UI: `/missions` gained an inline "Plan & dispatch" composer (title + goal textarea + one button) so the operator never needs to escape to `/agents` to launch a multi-agent mission; `/missions/$id` gained an "Orchestrator plan" panel above the existing timeline + graph showing the DAG with status pills + deps + an **Advance** button when work remains. Specialist child runs execute asynchronously via the existing `resume-runs` cron ÔÇö no new infra. **WHY:** the substrate was 95% there but the \_behavior* was missing ÔÇö until something planned a goal into a graph and dispatched it, "agent-native OS" was the marketing phrase for a single-agent planner-executor. Closes the first of three F-AGENT- gaps that block the autonomous-product-OS thesis. **Out of scope this turn (queued):** F-AGENT-2 (persistent agent memory + auto self-reflection + trust-arc auto-advance), F-AGENT-3 (event reactor + auto-pipelines), F-AGENT-4 (Swarm HUD), Restructure Phases 3ÔÇô4 (deferred per operator). **Files:** new `supabase/migrations/<ts>_mission_steps_and_orchestrator.sql` (+ a second migration patching the seed function with required `display_name`/`description` on `agent_tools` inserts), new `src/lib/ai/tools/orchestrator.server.ts`, new `src/lib/orchestrator.functions.ts`; edited `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts`, `src/lib/ai/loop.server.ts`, `src/routes/_authenticated.missions.index.tsx`, `src/routes/_authenticated.missions.$missionId.tsx`, `docs/planning/feature-backlog.md`, `plan.md`, `architecture/orchestration.md`.
- **2026-06-06 ÔÇö F-AGENT-2: Persistent agent memory + auto self-reflection + trust-arc auto-advance.** Second half of the agent-ecosystem bundle (F-AGENT-3 reactor + F-AGENT-4 Swarm HUD still queued). New `src/lib/ai/reflection.server.ts` exports `autoReflect()` (calls Gemini Flash through the chokepoint with `surface='agent', surface_ref='reflect:<slug>'`, expects strict JSON `{lesson, what_worked, what_to_change, importance:1-5}`, writes a `kind='reflection'` row to `agent_memory` with embedding + structured metadata ÔÇö `run_id`, `trace_id`, `goal`, `what_worked`, `what_to_change`) and `maybeAutoAdvanceArc()` (wraps the new `auto_advance_agent_arc(p_user_id, p_agent_id)` SECURITY DEFINER RPC). `loop.server.ts` calls both from BOTH finalize paths (fresh run + resumed run) when `!halted` ÔÇö halted runs skip reflection by design, so a governance halt never turns into a self-confirming lesson without operator review. `recallMemory()` now merges two sources: the existing `match_agent_memory` semantic search and the new `recent_agent_reflections` RPC (importance + recency ranked, top 3), deduped by content, capped at 8 ÔÇö so reflections surface even when the embedding store is sparse or the goal is novel. Two new tools in the registry: `memory.reflect` (category=memory; agent/operator on-demand reflection ÔÇö reads the current run's input/output if available, wraps `autoReflect`) and `memory.promote` (escalate a memory's scope agentÔåÆglobal so every agent in the workspace recalls it; e.g. "Q3 priority is retention"). Autonomy RPC: `auto_advance_agent_arc` SECURITY DEFINER promotes ObservingÔåÆProving at 5 clean completed runs and ProvingÔåÆTrusted at 20, only when no `agent_approvals.status='rejected'` row exists since the last `agent_autonomy.set_at`; never auto-promotes past Trusted (Ambient stays an explicit operator decision); never downgrades; tolerant of both legacy `status='complete'` (`runAgent` one-shot) and modern `status='completed'` (`loop.server.ts`); sets `set_by=NULL` on system promotion so the UI can distinguish operator vs system moves later. New `recent_agent_reflections(for_user, for_agent_slug, match_count)` SECURITY DEFINER RPC + new `listAgentReflections` server fn (`src/lib/agents.functions.ts`) power a **Recent reflections** panel on `/agents` showing each lesson with importance pill + what-worked / what-to-change sub-blocks pulled out of `metadata`. New cron route `/api/public/hooks/memory-tick` (daily 03:30 UTC via `memory-tick-daily` pg*cron job) deletes `importance <= 2 AND COALESCE(last_used_at, created_at) < now()-30d`, two split passes so the new `agent_memory_decay_idx` is actually used. Migration also fixed the long-standing `agent_memory` grants ÔÇö table was created without `GRANT SELECT/INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE ÔÇª TO authenticated`, only `sandbox_exec` had access; PostgREST + admin paths now work. Two new SECURITY DEFINER fns had EXECUTE revoked from PUBLIC (anon can't call them; only `authenticated` + `service_role`). **WHY:** F-AGENT-1 gave us a planner that decomposes goals ÔÇö F-AGENT-2 makes the resulting work \_compound*. Without persistent reflection every run started cold; without auto-advance the trust dial was operator-only, defeating the point of an autonomy ladder. Together these two close the "agents that learn and earn autonomy" half of the autonomous-product-OS thesis. **Out of scope (queued):** F-AGENT-3 (event reactor: `signal.created`ÔåÆDiscovery, `opportunity.scored>=80`ÔåÆStrategist, `prd.approved`ÔåÆOrchestrator + `/governance` subscriptions CRUD), F-AGENT-4 (Swarm HUD route with live missions / handoffs / pending approvals / auto-pipeline firings panels), Restructure Phases 3ÔÇô4. **Gotchas for the next tool:** (1) reflections write under the per-user supabase client RLS path, so they only land when `runId` exists; ad-hoc loop runs without an `agent_runs` row still reflect via the same helper but the `metadata.run_id` is null ÔÇö UI handles that. (2) `auto_advance_agent_arc` is called with `set_by=NULL` for system promotions; if you add a "promoted by" badge later, NULL = system, non-NULL = operator. (3) the cron-side admin client bypasses RLS for `memory-tick` deletes ÔÇö keep importanceÔëñ2 + 30d cutoffs tight so we never destroy operator-authored memories (`memory.remember` writes default importance=3, above the floor). (4) `memory.reflect` is intentionally `category=memory` (not `write`), so the autonomy dial cannot loosen it past `auto`; reflections should not be approval-gated. **Files:** new `src/lib/ai/reflection.server.ts`, new `src/routes/api/public/hooks/memory-tick.ts`, two new migrations (`<ts>_agent_memory_grants_and_autonomy_advance.sql` + `<ts>_revoke_public_execute_on_helpers.sql`); edited `src/lib/ai/loop.server.ts`, `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts`, `src/lib/agents.functions.ts`, `src/routes/_authenticated.agents.tsx`, `docs/planning/feature-backlog.md`, `plan.md`, `architecture/orchestration.md`.

- **2026-06-04 ÔÇö Bundle 5 Live Mission Graph (E6) shipped.** `/missions/$id` only had a linear timeline + per-hop progress panel; multi-agent missions couldn't be _seen_ as a graph, which is the literal success criterion for Step 5 of the build-order rollup ("graph updates in real time as agents act; clicking a node opens that agent's trace + cost + tokens + approval state"). Added a pure-SVG DAG component `src/components/cadence/MissionGraph.tsx` and mounted it above the existing timeline + hops list. **Nodes** = one per `agent_runs` row in the mission; status color + glyph + agent name + slug + status text. **Edges** = one per `agent_messages` row, drawn `source_run_id ÔåÆ consumed_by_run_id`; for in-flight handoffs not yet consumed, fall back to the earliest later hop targeting `to_agent_slug`. Edges are violet bezier paths with arrow markers + the message `kind` label. **Layout** = BFS-depth columns (root hops at column 0, each handoff bumps the child's column) ├ù chronological rows within column, so a single-agent mission renders 1 node / 0 edges and a Discovery ÔåÆ Strategist ÔåÆ Builder mission renders 3 nodes connected by 2 labelled edges; multiple outbound messages from the same parent stack as parallel children in the next column (E4 fan-out polish ready without a new tool). **Interaction**: nodes are real `role="button"` SVG groups with `onKeyDown` Enter/Space; clicking expands the matching hop card (adds to the existing `expanded` Set) and smooth-scrolls via `id="hop-{run_id}"` + `scroll-mt-24`. Re-uses the existing `refetchInterval: 2000` while mission `status='running'`/`queued`, so the graph fills in live. Pure read model ÔÇö no schema change, no new server fn, consumes the existing `getMission` payload. WHY: Step 5 of the build-order rollup needs the graph to be literally true, and Bundle 4's claim ("A2A is first-class, no human in the routing path") only becomes operator-legible once the routing is visible as a graph rather than a list. **Out of scope this turn:** pause/steer-from-graph controls, zoom/collapse for >20-node graphs, per-node cost/token rollup pill (needs `getMission` to surface it), explicit `agent.spawn` tool. **Files:** new `src/components/cadence/MissionGraph.tsx`; edited `src/routes/_authenticated.missions.$missionId.tsx`, `architecture/orchestration.md`, `docs/planning/feature-backlog.md`.

- **2026-06-04 ÔÇö Web access for agents shipped (Firecrawl-backed `web.*` tools).** Agents were siloed: a goal like _"scout how Linear's AI triage is positioned and give me a non-reactive one-pager"_ needed the public internet but had no tool to call, so they hallucinated or stopped short. Results re-enter the loop as untrusted input ÔÇö the next `callModel()` already runs them through pre-guardrails (PII / prompt-injection / secret keyword) per `architecture/runtime.md`, no new code required. - **2026-06-04 ÔÇö Bundle 3 Agent Trust Score + Autonomy Dial (C6) shipped.** New `agent_autonomy` table (one row per user+agent, arc enum `observing|proving|trusted|ambient`, owner-only RLS, standard GRANTs). - **2026-06-03 ÔÇö PM lifecycle tools shipped (`research.synthesize`, `prd.draft`, `backlog.prioritize`).** Added 3 PM-centric agentic tools to `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts` and seeded them into `agent_tools` for every existing user (and for new signups via the updated `seed_default_agent_tools(uuid)`), all default `confirm` mode. (1) `research.synthesize` ÔÇö pulls recent ungrouped `signals` (filterable by tag/sentiment/lookback), asks the model (via `callModel`, surface=`discovery`, `responseFormat=json_object`) to cluster them into 2ÔÇô6 cohesive themes, writes `themes` rows (severity 1ÔÇô5, confidence 0ÔÇô1, frequency = signal count) and links source signals via `signals.theme_id`. (2) `prd.draft(opportunity_id)` ÔÇö reads the opportunity, joins its `theme` + top 8 supporting signals, asks the model (surface=`prd`) to draft a structured PRD (Problem / Target user / Goals / Non-goals / Stories / Solution sketch / Success metrics / Risks) and writes a `prds` row in `draft` status with `model` recorded. (3) `backlog.prioritize` ÔÇö for each backlog opportunity, gathers supporting-signal count + recency (last 7d), asks the model to re-score ICE (1ÔÇô10 integers) with rationale, updates `opportunities.{impact,confidence,ease}` (ice_score is a generated column so it recomputes), returns the new ranked list with rationales. All three flow through the AI chokepoint so they hit guardrails + budgets + tracing, and through the agent loop they pick up `runId`/`stepIndex` automatically for idempotent retry on resume. No per-agent assignment needed ÔÇö the loop filters `TOOL_REGISTRY` by what the user has enabled, so Discovery Scout / PRD Writer / Strategist see them immediately. Closes the Define + Plan halves of the Bundle 6 lifecycle slice that previously had only the GitHub-issue write on the Build edge. Files: `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts`, migration `seed_pm_lifecycle_tools(uuid)` + folded into `seed_default_agent_tools(uuid)` with a backfill loop.
- **2026-06-03 ÔÇö FND-RUNTIME 0.9 runtime instrumentation + N1 `github.issue.create` shipped.** Added `src/lib/runtime/idempotency.server.ts` (`withIdempotency(scope,key,userId,runId,fn)` ÔåÆ execute ÔåÆ INSERT-on-conflict-fall-back-to-cached against the new `idempotency_keys` table). Refactored `src/lib/ai/loop.server.ts` so both `runAgentLoop()` (fresh) and new exported `resumeAgentLoop(runId)` (rehydrates from latest `agent_run_checkpoints` row) feed a shared `executeLoop()`; every iteration upserts a checkpoint _before_ the provider call (so a `GovernanceHaltError` mid-stream never re-bills on resume) and wraps tool execution in `withIdempotency` keyed `tool:{runId}:{stepIndex}:{toolName}` ÔÇö replaying a step short-circuits to the cached result instead of re-invoking the side-effecting tool. Added per-workspace **backpressure** (default 5 concurrent `running` runs); over-cap missions insert as `status='queued'` and are promoted by the new `/api/public/hooks/resume-runs` sweeper, which also resumes `running` runs whose `last_checkpoint_at` is >2 min stale (worker eviction). Sweeper is `pg_cron`-driven every minute against the stable preview URL. Added **`github.issue.create`** agentic tool to `TOOL_REGISTRY` (category `write`, default `confirm` mode): writes to the single allow-listed `GITHUB_REPO` env, validated `owner/name` format, idempotent via caller-supplied `idempotency_key` (e.g. PRD id) so re-execution from a checkpoint never double-creates an issue. ToolCtx extended with optional `runId` + `stepIndex` so future tools can key their own idempotency without re-deriving. Files: `src/lib/runtime/idempotency.server.ts` (new), `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts`, `src/lib/ai/loop.server.ts`, `src/routes/api/public/hooks/resume-runs.ts` (new), plus a `pg_cron` migration scheduling `resume-runs` every minute. - **2026-06-03 ÔÇö FND-RUNTIME 0.9 foundation landed (decision + schema + secrets).** Wrote `docs/decisions/durable-runtime.md` selecting a **DB-backed durable job table** over Cloudflare Queues ÔÇö rationale: matches existing `/api/public/hooks/*` + `pg_cron` + tenancy patterns; zero new infra/runtime/auth model; portable off Cloudflare; visible to the human governor as ordinary rows. Applied a migration adding (1) `agent_run_checkpoints` ÔÇö append-only, one row per loop iteration, `UNIQUE (run_id, step_index)`, `state JSONB`, full tenancy keys, RLS scoped to `auth.uid()`; (2) `idempotency_keys` ÔÇö `UNIQUE (scope, key)` dedup table for `/api/public/hooks/*` ticks (`tick:{hook}:{run_id}:{step_index}`) and tool execution (`tool:{run_id}:{step_index}:{tool_name}`) so a resumed step never re-executes a side-effecting tool; (3) `agent_runs.step_index` + `last_checkpoint_at` for heartbeat + resume cursor.
