> This is the earlier build (the "vibe-coded" source). **It is a reuse reference, not the plan.** Mine it for what survives the stress-test; supersede entries as they're rebuilt into section 4. Do not treat anything here as current truth without checking the code.

- **Foundation** ÔÇö Supabase auth (email + Google OAuth), `profiles`, workspaces + extended `projects`, persistent SSE chat with workspace grounding, model-agnostic router with per-surface defaults, command palette (ÔîÿK), Mission Control widgets, OKLCH dark theme, RLS, loader+Suspense pattern, route boundaries, global auth middleware. _(Largely reusable.)_
- **Discovery & specs** ÔÇö `signals` ingest (paste/CSV, chunked inserts; sentiment on insert), clustering (k-medoid + synthesis with `evidence_ids[]`), themes ÔåÆ ICE opportunities, one-click PRD ÔåÆ Tiptap with `/ai` slash menu, `prd_versions` autosave + diff, early pgvector RAG (512/64 chunks, 1536-d). _(Reusable; this is the first-slice base.)_
- **Planning & meeting intelligence** ÔÇö Now/Next/Later board (`@dnd-kit`). _(Tail of this legacy entry was lost in an earlier edit collision that spliced the ┬º6 heading mid-line ÔÇö recover details from git history if ever needed.)_

## 6. Product-agent roster (re-examined: explicit vs. implicit)

**The question:** is a fixed roster of 16 named agents right? **Answer:** no ÔÇö split it. Use a small set of **durable, named lifecycle agents** (explicit, one owner per stage) plus an orchestrator that **dynamically spawns ephemeral specialist sub-agents** for sub-tasks (implicit). Fixed seats for micro-roles create clutter; dynamic sub-agents scale with the work.

**6 outcome-focused durable agents (explicit, one per lifecycle band):**

The roster is kept narrow and delivery-oriented. Each agent owns a clear band of the product lifecycle. Fixed seats for micro-roles are avoided ÔÇö those collapse into ephemeral specialists.

| Agent            | Lifecycle band                                                  | Owns                                                                                                             | Primary pain point addressed                                    |
| ---------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Orchestrator** | All stages                                                      | Mission coordination, spawns ephemeral specialists, manages approval routing, parallelism                        | Coordination overhead, context loss between stages              |
| **Discovery**    | S1 Signal Capture + S2 Audio Sync                               | Signal Ingest (Zendesk/Intercom/Slack), clustering opportunities, WhisperFlow transcription and audio extraction | Shallow discovery, anecdotal signals, missing verbal alignments |
| **Strategist**   | S3 ICE Prioritization + S4 Spec Definition + S5 Sprint Planning | Opportunity scoring, cited PRD generation, Linear/GitHub Issues sync, dependency-aware task graphs               | Spec drafting overhead, weak prioritization, feature factories  |
| **Builder**      | S6 Agentic Build + S7 Visual QA + S8 Safe Release               | Multi-file coding, file claims ledger, sandbox previews, PR merge checks and deploy monitoring                   | Developer bottlenecks, styling drift, release quality checks    |
| **Growth**       | S9 GTM Launch                                                   | Outbound changelogs, blog posts, Slack notifications and release announcements                                   | Launch overhead, delayed go-to-market communication             |
| **Analyst**      | S10 Support Triage + S11 Cohort Analytics + S12 Learn & Reflect | Support ticket routing to S1, adoption funnels, performance metrics vs PRD specs, Product Memory                 | Closed-loop support, un-measured features, memory decay         |

**Ephemeral specialists (spawned by Orchestrator per task):** competitor scan, UX critique, stakeholder brief, data analysis, security review, code review, and any other short-lived specialist. They inherit the chokepoint, tool allow-list, and governance. No permanent seats for micro-roles.

**Persona mapping:**

- **P1 (Director / VP of Product)**: strategic oversight, budget controls, audit log reviews, portfolio health, uses Analyst + Orchestrator.
- **P2 (Lead / Senior PM)**: daily operator, runs swarm briefs, PRD editor, discovery feeds, uses Discovery + Strategist + Analyst.
- **P3 (Engineering Lead)**: code review, Builder agent claims review, CI verification, uses Builder.
- **P4 (UX/UI Designer)**: sandbox preview validation, style token audit, uses Builder (Visual QA).
- **P5 (GTM Lead)**: launch copywriting, distribution approvals, uses Growth.
- **P6 (Support Lead)**: triage validation, bug signal loops, uses Analyst.

Schema per agent: `slug, name, system_prompt, tool_allowlist[], default_model, temperature/top_p/seed, max_tokens, schedule_cron?, approval_mode (auto|confirm|review), memory_enabled`. Roster changes need a migration + a build-order entry.

---

## 7. Testing strategy

- **Unit:** pricing math, each guardrail rule kind, RAG chunker boundaries, ICE/cron/date helpers.
- **Integration:** chokepoint (one `ai_events` row + trace; budget throws before provider; cache short-circuits but logs; guardrail block aborts + logs; ticks idempotent); orchestration (parallel sessions isolated; checkpoints resume; cancellation saves partial trace); RLS isolation across products/workspaces.
- **Autonomous build/test loop:** the Builder agent's output must pass the QA agent's generated tests before Ship; a failing eval suite ("Cadence core") blocks deploy (ÔëÑ10-point regression on the 0ÔÇô100 scale, without override ÔÇö KI-14).
- **E2E:** intent ÔåÆ discover ÔåÆ define ÔåÆ plan ÔåÆ build ÔåÆ test ÔåÆ ship, watched in the orchestration view; multi-product isolation; ÔîÿK across routes; `/observe` renders on seeded data.
- **Manual QA before release:** auth + tenancy isolation; every route empty/partial/full; AI message contract present ([`design.md`](./design.md)); guardrail block works; budget breach is friendly; light-theme Cohere editorial contrast.

---

## 8. Lessons learned (kept from the legacy build)

One AI chokepoint paid for itself (judge added in half a day). Loader + `useSuspenseQuery` killed `useEffect+fetch` regressions. OKLCH tokens ended dark-mode contrast bugs. Bugs fixed: name-vs-email leak; duplicate agent fan-out (advisory lock); action-item due-date glitch; Notion BFS reorder; trace recursion blow-up; cache cross-user poisoning (salted key); CSV params cap (chunked inserts). Known limits: clustering degrades past ~1000 signals/run; Studio truncates files >2k lines; Docs sync drops comments; `model_pricing` hand-maintained.

---

## 9. Out of scope (for now)

Fine-tuning workflows from `ai_events`; cross-workspace vector sharing; public agent/skill-pack marketplace; cross-workspace SSO; fully autonomous _strategic_ decisions (strategic conclusions keep a human gate by design ÔÇö tactical ones may auto-apply). These are deliberate exclusions, revisited when the core loop is solid.

**H3 ┬À Scheduling (calendar-aware work blocks) ÔÇö SHIPPED.** Agent proposes deep-work blocks into free time within the operator's working hours, fitting the task around meetings and respecting focus. Built: (1) `proposeWorkBlocks` server fn in `calendar.functions.ts` ÔÇö reads open deep-work tasks (is_deep_work=true, status != done) from the `tasks` table, fetches the user's working-hours bounds from the profile, queries calendar events for the next 7 days (daysAhead param), and uses a simple greedy algorithm (30-min slot buckets, skip weekends/out-of-hours, skip conflicts) to place one block per task into the first-fit free slot. Returns a list of WorkBlock (start_at, end_at, title, label with formatted time). Boundaries are soft (a packed calendar yields fewer blocks; no forced fit). (2) UI affordance in `CalendarPanel.tsx` ÔÇö a "Plan deep work" button in the action bar triggers the proposal, showing a panel with the proposed blocks + "Add to calendar" per-block buttons; a visual state change (color shift) marks added blocks; a "Re-plan ┬À new proposal" option re-runs the algorithm (useful if the calendar changed). (3) Mutations integrate with the existing `createCalendarEvent` so added blocks sync two-way with the user's calendar provider (Google/Microsoft). **Scope:** the proposal algorithm is honest (no speculative ML or scoring); the 7-day window and 30-min bucket size are sensible defaults (tunable via params). Deferred: adaptive working-hour inference, multi-day blocks, and conflict re-routing (schedule around soft-constraints rather than hard skip). **Verification:** `bun test` 163 green, `bun run build` green, `eslint` clean, dev server boots. Manual: seeded workspace with 3 open deep-work tasks + a calendar with 6 events ÔåÆ "Plan deep work" proposes 2 blocks (Tue afternoon, Thu morning, both 60-min, both fit free slots, both fit within 09:00ÔÇô18:00). **Files:** `src/lib/calendar.functions.ts` (proposeWorkBlocks + type), `src/components/knowledge/CalendarPanel.tsx` (affordance + mutations + UI), dashboard/this log.

**U6 ┬À Workspace data export (data portability), CORE SHIPPED (autonomous overnight cycle 1, 2026-06-18).** The trust escape-hatch: Settings > Data downloads the entire workspace as one JSON file. Built: (1) `exportWorkspace` server fn in `projects.functions.ts` (mirrors B5 `exportProduct` at workspace scope): resolves the active workspace (passed from the client, falling back to first membership), gathers projects (by workspace_id), signals/opportunities/specs(`prds`)/tasks (by project_id across the workspace's projects, guarded against the empty-projects case so it never issues an empty `in()`), and the user's own `learnings` + `agent_memory` (owner-scoped by user_id). RLS scopes every read to the caller; returns a JSON-safe shape with a per-section `counts` map. No migration (read-only). (2) `DataExportCard.tsx` in `src/components/settings/` + a new "Data" tab on `/settings`: a calm-front card that calls the fn, downloads `cadence-workspace-export-<date>.json`, and toasts the record count. It passes the active workspace id so multi-workspace users export the right one. **Adversarial review folded 2 fixes:** the empty-projects `.in([])` guard, and the active-workspace-id pass-through (it was exporting the first workspace, not the active one). **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `eslint` clean, `bun run build` green. **Pending founder publish + live verify** (not deployed yet). **Remaining (ÔùÉ):** per-section selective export + an export audit-log. **Files:** `src/lib/projects.functions.ts`, `src/components/settings/DataExportCard.tsx`, `src/routes/_authenticated.settings.tsx`, `docs/features/u6-data-export.md`, dashboard/this log.

**R3 ┬À Notifications, in-app Attention feed CORE SHIPPED (autonomous overnight cycle 2, 2026-06-18).** The operator hears about what needs them, in one place. Built: (1) `getNotifications` server fn in a new `src/lib/notifications.functions.ts`: derives a unified feed live from the loop's own state, with no new table: pending tool-call approvals (`agent_approvals` status=pending), a stalled loop (`agent_runs` running/queued past the 30-minute window), and spend nearing or over a cap (`ai_budgets` daily/monthly vs `alert_at_pct`). Read-only, RLS-scoped by user_id; each probe degrades to a safe default so the feed can never break its surface. Returns a severity-sorted `AppNotification[]` (action > warning > info) with a deep-link href per item, plus a `count` for a future bell badge. (2) `NotificationsPanel.tsx` + a new "Attention" tab on the Engine Room (`/govern?tab=attention`): a calm feed of severity-coded cards, each linking to its home (approvals / spend / loop-health), with an "All clear" empty state. **Adversarial review folded 1 fix:** placed Attention second (not first) so the default-selected leftmost tab stays Controls (no behavior change; the default landing is left to a founder taste call). **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `eslint` clean, `bun run build` green. **Pending founder publish + live verify.** **Remaining (ÔùÉ):** email + digests, per-user notification prefs, and the global bell badge. **Files:** `src/lib/notifications.functions.ts`, `src/components/governance/NotificationsPanel.tsx`, `src/routes/_authenticated.govern.tsx`, `docs/features/r3-notifications.md`, dashboard/this log.

**P7 ┬À Incidents log, read-only CORE SHIPPED (autonomous overnight cycle 3, 2026-06-18).** A record when something goes wrong, instead of failures vanishing into the logs. Built: (1) `getIncidents` server fn in a new `src/lib/incidents.functions.ts`: derives a read-only "what went wrong" log with no new table from confirmed sources: `agent_approvals` (status=failed, by user_id) for failed tool executions, and `event_queue` (rows with a non-null error, scoped to the resolved default workspace) for errored auto-pipelines. Merged newest-first, capped at 40; each execution carries its `trace_id`. (2) `IncidentsPanel.tsx` + a new "Incidents" tab on the Engine Room (`/govern?tab=incidents`): cards with the error detail, a timestamp, and a "View trace" link per execution; "No incidents" empty state. **Adversarial review folded 1 fix:** explicit workspace scoping on `event_queue` (matching the reactor pattern) rather than relying on RLS alone. **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `eslint` clean, `bun run build` green. **Pending founder publish + live verify.** **Remaining (ÔùÉ):** guardrail/cost incident sources + a persistent incidents table for manual logging. **Files:** `src/lib/incidents.functions.ts`, `src/components/governance/IncidentsPanel.tsx`, `src/routes/_authenticated.govern.tsx`, `docs/features/p7-incidents.md`, dashboard/this log.

**C4/E7 ┬À Agent inspector (run history), CORE SHIPPED (autonomous overnight cycle 4, 2026-06-18).** See what each agent has actually been doing, not just its trust score. Built: (1) `getAgentRuns` server fn in a new `src/lib/agent-runs.functions.ts`: reads `agent_runs` filtered by user_id (RLS + explicit, defense-in-depth) and agent_id, newest-first, capped at 25; returns each run's status, mission_id, step_index, created_at. Read-only, no migration. (2) `AgentInspector.tsx` in `src/components/cockpit/` + a one-line mount in `AgentsPanel` (Missions > Agents, below the trust dial): an agent dropdown + that agent's recent run list (status, mission, step, time), with a "no runs yet" empty state. **Adversarial review: clean** (hooks kept unconditional before the early return; RLS + explicit user_id filter; schema grounded against `agent_runs` before building). **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `eslint` clean, `bun run build` green. **Pending founder publish + live verify.** **Remaining (ÔùÉ):** the shared/private memory inspector (needs agent-scope columns on `agent_memory` confirmed live). **Files:** `src/lib/agent-runs.functions.ts`, `src/components/cockpit/AgentInspector.tsx`, `src/components/cockpit/AgentsPanel.tsx`, `docs/features/c4-e7-agent-inspector.md`, dashboard/this log.

**C4/E7 ┬À Agent memory inspector, COMPLETES C4/E7 (autonomous overnight cycle 5, 2026-06-18).** What each agent knows, alongside its run history. Built: (1) `getAgentMemory` server fn (in `agent-runs.functions.ts`): returns the selected agent's memories, its own (private, `agent_id=agentId`) plus the shared/global pool (`scope=global`), via two injection-safe `.eq()` queries merged and deduped by id (no `.or()` string interpolation, so a crafted agentId cannot rewrite the filter), RLS-scoped. (2) extended `AgentInspector.tsx` with a "What this agent knows" section below the run history: each memory labelled shared or private, with its kind + content. **Adversarial review: clean** (injection-safe two-query merge; hooks kept unconditional). **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `eslint` clean, `bun run build` green. With this, C4/E7 is complete (run history + shared/private memory). **Pending founder publish + live verify** (incl. confirming `agent_memory.agent_id` matches the swarm agent id). **Files:** `src/lib/agent-runs.functions.ts`, `src/components/cockpit/AgentInspector.tsx`, `docs/features/c4-e7-agent-inspector.md`, dashboard/this log.

The cascade stops the resume cron resuming orphaned child runs (required for correctness, not cosmetics), releases held Build file claims (the `release_claims_for_terminal_run` trigger skips `cancelled`, so locks would otherwise orphan), and clears pending approvals. **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `bun run build` green, the 3 touched files lint clean (the repo-wide `bun run lint` shows pre-existing prettier debt in untouched files, flagged in the report; not mass-reformatted). **Adversarial review** folded a TOCTOU guard (only flip to `cancelled` if still non-terminal, so a mission that finishes in the readÔåÆwrite window keeps its honest state) and confirmed `completed_at` does not corrupt the analytics completion metric (it filters on `status='completed'`). **Permission policy hardening + capture (autonomous overnight cycle 13, 2026-06-18, founder-requested).** The founder was getting a permission prompt on every read/edit/command. Root cause: a session reads the `.claude/settings.local.json` of the directory it is LAUNCHED from; this session runs from the repo ROOT, but the bypass config only existed in the WORKTREE's copy, so the root session prompted on everything. **Fix:** (1) set `defaultMode: bypassPermissions` + the broad allow + destructive deny + both directories in the **root** `.claude/settings.local.json` (local, gitignored, per-machine); (2) added a shared `permissions` allow/deny block to the **committed** `.claude/settings.json` so the lists travel with the repo and cover regular daytime builds too (no `defaultMode` there ÔÇö bypass stays a per-machine opt-in, never committed); (3) wrote [`docs/operations/permissions.md`](docs/operations/permissions.md) capturing the two-layer model, the deny-list floor, and the learnings (which settings file a session reads, settings read at startup, the worktree gotcha); linked it from `autonomous-build-loop.md` ┬º11 + CLAUDE.md read order. No app code. **Files:** `.claude/settings.json` (committed), `docs/operations/permissions.md` (new), `docs/operations/autonomous-build-loop.md`, `CLAUDE.md`, report, this log. (Local `.claude/settings.local.json` updated on the machine; gitignored, not committed.)

**R3 global Attention bell (autonomous overnight cycle 15, 2026-06-18).** Advances `R3`: the Attention feed only surfaced "what needs you" once you were inside the Engine Room; this gives it a doorway from every screen. Built `AttentionBell.tsx` (`src/components/cadence/`), a persistent bell in the `TopBar` (rendered next to the AmbientChip, so it appears on every route): it carries the live count of what needs you (approvals waiting, spend nearing a cap, a stalled loop), tinted by the most urgent item (action amber > warning rose > info muted), and links to `/govern?tab=attention`. It is quiet (no badge) when all clear. It reuses `getNotifications` under the **shared `["notifications"]` query key**, so when the Attention panel is also mounted there is one fetch, not two (the same cache-sharing the Approvals badge uses); a failed fetch degrades to "all clear" so the bell can never break the top bar. **Design call (no double-count):** the app already had a Trust-row "Approvals" badge (`getNeedsYou`) that badges the Approvals *nav item* (`?tab=approvals`); the bell badges the *whole* Attention feed (`?tab=attention`). They are deliberately distinct surfaces, so when only approvals exist they agree (reinforcement) and when an alert also exists the bell reads higher; I did not merge or remove the working Approvals badge. **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `bun run build` green, both touched files lint clean (eslint + prettier), humanization clean (the one em-dash I authored fixed; the `TopBar` header's pre-existing dashes are outside my diff and left untouched per the surgical rule). **Adversarial review** folded one fix: dropped `role="status"` from the actionable `<a>` so the bell keeps its link semantics for screen readers (a live-region role would have overridden the link). **Pending publish + live verify.** **Files:** `src/components/cadence/AttentionBell.tsx` (new), `src/components/cadence/TopBar.tsx`, `docs/features/r3-notifications.md`, dashboard (R3 row + header), report, session-decisions, this log.

**P7 guardrail-block incident source (autonomous overnight cycle 16, 2026-06-18).** Advances `P7`: the Incidents log derived from two sources (failed tool executions + errored pipelines); it now also surfaces **guardrail blocks**. Extended `getIncidents` (`incidents.functions.ts`) with a third source reading the existing `guardrail_hits` table (no migration) filtered to `action = "block"` and scoped by `user_id`: only a block is "what went wrong" (the rule actually stopped an AI call), so the softer `warn`/`redact` actions (the call still runs) are intentionally excluded so routine governance is not mislabelled an incident. Each card reads `Blocked by guardrail: <rule>` with which side it fired on (a blocked prompt vs a withheld response); it deliberately **omits the raw `matched` payload** so nothing sensitive lands in a list view, and carries no trace link (`guardrail_hits` keys to an `event_id`, not a trace). Added `"guardrail"` to the `IncidentKind` union, which (via the exhaustive `Record<Incident["kind"], string>` in `IncidentsPanel.tsx`) forced the matching `Guardrail` label, plus updated the empty-state copy. **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `bun run build` green, both touched files lint + prettier + humanization clean. **Adversarial review:** RLS double-scoped (`user_id` + policy), `matched` excluded, block-only filter, null traceId consistent with pipeline incidents; clean, no fix. **Pending publish + live verify.** **Files:** `src/lib/incidents.functions.ts`, `src/components/governance/IncidentsPanel.tsx`, `docs/features/p7-incidents.md`, dashboard (P7 row + header), report, this log.

Unassigned signals (no product, e.g. the workspace ingest webhook) live in the all-products view, never hidden. **Deferred (founder-gated):** the auto-cluster cron (continuous incremental re-cluster) commits recurring AI spend, so it stays queued. **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `bun run build` green, all 4 touched files eslint + prettier clean, my additions humanization-clean (pre-existing dashes in these design-reference-ported files are the deferred HUMAN-SWEEP, not touched). **Adversarial review** folded one fix: a signal whose theme is outside the current product scope is shown as a standalone row rather than vanishing from the view (data is never lost). **F-AGENTS-MENTIONABLE: direct specialist dispatch via @mention (autonomous overnight cycle 19, 2026-06-18).** Implements the composer affordance for naming a specialist by mention, skipping the orchestrator's planning round-trip. **The insight:** a mention is an unambiguous intent (the user *chose* the agent), so it avoids the classifier model call and pre-plans a single-step DAG directly. **Architecture:** `parseAgentMentions()` regex extracts `@slug` tokens at word boundaries (email-safe: requires preceding whitespace); roster lookup against enabled agents (excluding orchestrator) is O(1) per candidate; first match wins. `stripMention()` removes the matched token so the goal text reads as a clean instruction (the agent is already chosen). If a mention resolves, chat.ts skips the classifier, pre-creates a `mission_step` with `status:"planned"`, and calls `advanceMissionCore()` directly (idempotent, never blocks the reply). The resume-runs cron picks up the step and executes it; `maybeCompleteMission` closes the mission when the step is terminal because `steps.length > 0`. **No lifecycle changes neededÔÇöthe orchestrator's deterministic advance machinery handles all paths identically.** Bare mention (no goal) falls back to regular chat. **Gate:** `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean, `bun run build` green (869 lines, 114.3 KB server asset), lint clean on touched file (pre-existing debt in design-reference files flagged separately). **Adversarial review:** Regex is slug-constrained (no ReDoS), stripMention interpolates safely (slug is [a-z-] only), roster lookup is RLS-scoped, bare-mention fallback is defensive, no silent failures. Clean, no fix. **Pending publish + live verify.** **Files:** `src/routes/api/chat.ts` (parseAgentMentions + stripMention + mention parse + preflight + step creation + dispatch + UI text), docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md (F-AGENTS-MENTIONABLE Ô£à), report, this log.
